## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the right-hand side of a population dynamics ODE. The presence of both t and P suggests possible non-autonomous dynamics such as seasonal forcing, time-varying carrying capacity, or harvesting schedules.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth (differential form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/population modeling)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant yield harvesting)
- Logistic with proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (effort-based harvesting)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (periodic environmental variation)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized growth with flexible inflection point)
- Time-dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (changing environment over time)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial approximation of density effects)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional growth kinetics)
- Delayed logistic proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t * P (time as proxy for delayed feedback)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P (dP_dt ∝ P) → exponential/Malthusian regime; look for c0*P terms as base growth
- Quadratic in P (terms like P² with negative coefficient) → density-dependent regulation, logistic-type saturation
- Cubic in P (positive P, negative P², or P(P-a)(K-P) structure) → Allee effect with bistability
- Multiplicative time-population coupling (t*P terms) → non-autonomous dynamics, changing environment
- Trigonometric functions of t multiplied by growth terms → seasonal/periodic environmental forcing
- Logarithmic dependence on P (P*log(P) terms) → Gompertz-type growth with log-linear feedback
- Constant additive/subtractive terms independent of P → external harvesting, immigration, or stocking
- Fractional powers of P (P^c with 0<c<1) → sub-linear growth suggesting resource limitation at individual level
- Ratio of polynomials in P → functional response or interference competition effects
- Exponential decay in t multiplied by growth terms → transient environmental effects or resource depletion

# Analysis of Candidate Formulas vs Ground Truth

## Ground Truth (GT)
The GT expression is:
$$0.11781609*(1 - e^{-0.027228*P})*P + 0.11781609*P*e^{-0.027228*t}$$

Expanding this:
$$0.11781609*P - 0.11781609*P*e^{-0.027228*P} + 0.11781609*P*e^{-0.027228*t}$$

This has three terms:
1. A constant times P: `c0*P`
2. A term with P times exp(-c2*P): `-c0*P*exp(-c2*P)`
3. A term with P times exp(-c4*t): `c3*P*exp(-c4*t)`

So the GT structure is: **P*A + P*B*exp(C*t) + P*D*exp(E*P)** where A, B, C, D, E are specific constants.

Specifically: `P*0.11781609 + P*0.11781609*exp(-0.027228*t) + P*(-0.11781609)*exp(-0.027228*P)`

## Checking Candidates

Let me check which candidates can match the structure `P*c + P*c*exp(c*t) + P*c*exp(c*P)`.

**Candidate 17: `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3*exp(P*c4)`**

This has exactly three terms:
- `P*c0` → matches `0.11781609*P` with c0 = 0.11781609
- `P*c1*exp(c2*t)` → matches `0.11781609*P*exp(-0.027228*t)` with c1 = 0.11781609, c2 = -0.027228
- `P*c3*exp(P*c4)` → matches `-0.11781609*P*exp(-0.027228*P)` with c3 = -0.11781609, c4 = -0.027228

**This is a perfect match!** ✓

Let me verify a few others that also contain this structure:

This simplifies to `P*(c0+c3) + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c4*exp(P*c5)`, which has the same structure as #17 (c0 and c3 combine into one constant). ✓ Also matches.

Same as #16 with an extra constant P term. Also matches (set c6=0 or absorb). ✓

**GT:** `0.11781609251252895*(1 - exp(-0.027228491244958825*P))*P + 0.11781609251252895*P*exp(-0.027228491244958825*t)`

Expanding the GT:
`0.11781609251252895*P - 0.11781609251252895*P*exp(-0.027228491244958825*P) + 0.11781609251252895*P*exp(-0.027228491244958825*t)`

So GT = `a*P + b*P*exp(d*P) + e*P*exp(f*t)` where:
- a = 0.11781609...
- b = -0.11781609...
- d = -0.027228...
- e = 0.11781609...
- f = -0.027228...

The GT has three basis terms (all multiplied by P):
1. **P** (constant coefficient)
2. **P·exp(c·P)** (exponential in P)
3. **P·exp(c·t)** (exponential in t)

Now I'll check each candidate to see if it can reduce to exactly these three terms by setting free constants appropriately.

**Key structural requirement:** The candidate must contain exactly these basis functions (or be reducible to them). Extra terms must be eliminable by setting their coefficients to 0.

Let me re-examine **Candidate 21** more carefully:
`P**2*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2 + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + P*c5*log(c6*exp(P*c7) + 1)`

Can we NOT zero c5 and instead make log(c6*exp(P*c7) + 1) = exp(d*P)? No, these are fundamentally different functions. But wait — can we use the P²*c0*exp(c1*t) term? Set c1=0: P²*c0 + P*c2 + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + P*c5*log(c6*exp(P*c7)+1). Still no P*exp(c*P) term. This candidate cannot produce P*exp(c*P). **NO MATCH.**

Actually wait, let me reconsider. If c6 is very large and c7 is the right value, log(c6*exp(P*c7) + 1) ≈ log(c6) + P*c7 for large c6. But this is an approximation, not exact. The function log(c6*exp(x)+1) is never exactly equal to exp(d*x) for any constants. So Candidate 21 is indeed NO MATCH.
